// If portReference has an int value, it is treated as a literal, and simply returns that value.\n109: // If portReference is a string, an attempt is first made to parse it as an integer.  If that fails,\n110: // an attempt is made to find a port with the same name in the container spec.\n111: // If a port with the same name is found, it's ContainerPort value is returned. \tonRepeatedHeartbeatFailure func()\n1065: \n1066: \t// podManager stores the desired set of admitted pods and mirror pods that the kubelet should be\n1067: \t// running. The actual set of running pods is stored on the podWorkers. The manager is populated\n1068: \t// by the kubelet config loops which abstracts receiving configuration from many different sources\n1069: \t// (api for regular pods, local filesystem or http for static pods). The manager may be consulted\n1070: \t// by other components that need to see the set of desired pods. Note that not all desired pods are\n1071: \t// running, and not all running pods are in the podManager - for instance, force deleting a pod\n1072: \t// from the apiserver will remove it from the podManager, but the pod may still be terminating and\n1073: \t// tracked by the podWorkers. Components that need to know the actual consumed resources of the\n1074: \t// node or are driven by podWorkers and the sync*Pod methods (status, volume, stats) should also\n1075: \t// consult the podWorkers when reconciling.\n1076: \t//\n1077: \t// TODO: review all kubelet components that need the actual set of pods (vs the desired set)\n1078: \t// and update them to use podWorkers instead of podManager. This may introduce latency in some\n1079: \t// methods, but avoids race conditions and correctly accounts for terminating pods that have\n1080: \t// been force deleted or static pods that have been updated.\n1081: \t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/116970\n1082: \tpodManager kubepod.Manager\n1083: \n1084: \t// podWorkers is responsible for driving the lifecycle state machine of each pod. The worker is\n1085: \t// notified of config changes, updates, periodic reconciliation, container runtime updates, and\n1086: \t// evictions of all desired pods and will invoke reconciliation methods per pod in separate\n1087: \t// goroutines. The podWorkers are authoritative in the kubelet for what pods are actually being\n1088: \t// run and their current state:\n1089: \t//\n1090: \t// * syncing: pod should be running (syncPod)\n1091: \t// * terminating: pod should be stopped (syncTerminatingPod)\n1092: \t// * terminated: pod should have all resources cleaned up (syncTerminatedPod)\n1093: \t//\n1094: \t// and invoke the handler methods that correspond to each state. Components within the\n1095: \t// kubelet that need to know the phase of the pod in order to correctly set up or tear down\n1096: \t// resources must consult the podWorkers.\n1097: \t//\n1098: \t// Once a pod has been accepted by the pod workers, no other pod with that same UID (and\n1099: \t// name+namespace, for static pods) will be started until the first pod has fully terminated\n1100: \t// and been cleaned up by SyncKnownPods. There are several constraints:\n1258: \t// 1. nodeMonitorGracePeriod must be N times more than nodeStatusUpdateFrequency, where\n1259: \t//    N means number of retries allowed for kubelet to post node status. Kubelet may fail to update node status reliably if the value is too small,\n1265: \t//    as it takes time to gather all necessary node information.\n1266: \tnodeStatusUpdateFrequency time.Duration\n1267: \n1268: \t// nodeStatusReportFrequency is the frequency that kubelet posts node\n1269: \t// status to master.
